As for adhesion of the scrotum to the testicle.
This adhesion occurs in those whose foreskin is intact and has not been circumcised, and it may occur due to a wound or tumor. It should be scraped off with a blunt probe until the ligament dissolves and the scrotum is freed on all sides.
If it is difficult to distinguish them upon examination, a portion of the scrotum and foreskin should be scraped off. The foreskin is thin, so it may easily be pierced due to its thinness. Then, separate the foreskin from the scrotum with a thin linen cloth moistened in cold water so that they do not adhere again.
It is then treated with an astringent solution until it heals.
Chapter Fifty-Seven.
On the Purification of Boys and the Treatment of Ailments Affecting Them.
Circumcision is nothing more than the separation of a connection, like other surgical procedures. However, since it is an act of our will and its use is particularly common in boys, we must strive to perform it in the best way possible.
The easiest path to safety, I say, is that the ancients did not mention circumcision in any of their writings because it was not practiced in their laws. It is something we have acquired.
This is through experience, for I have found that the majority of artisans and barbers use purification with a syringe and scissors, employing forceps and ligation with thread and cutting with a nail. I have tried all these methods.
I have not found anything better than purification with scissors and ligation with thread because purification with a syringe often causes the skin to retract, as the foreskin has two layers, and the upper layer may be cut while the lower layer remains.
This often necessitates another cut and renewed pain. Purification with forceps does not guarantee the cutting of the tip of the penis because it may enter the hole. As for purification with a nail, the skin may slip, ruining your work, or the boy's skin may be naturally short...
Very often they are born this way and do not need to be cleansed, and I have seen this. As for cleansing with scissors and ligature with thread, experience has revealed its benefit because the scissors cut proportionally due to the blade on top being like the blade on the bottom.
So when you squeeze your hand, the blades being proportional, cut to an equal measure and at the same time, so that the ligature becomes like a wall for the skin of the penis on all sides, and no error occurs with it whatsoever. The first step in this procedure is to trick the boy.
Especially if he is one who understands a little, you should make him believe that you are only tying the thread to his penis and leaving it until another day; then rejoice him and delight him in every way that he can comprehend, and then have him stand upright before you.
Do not have him sitting down; hide the scissors in your sleeve or under your foot so that the boy does not see them at all, nor any of the instruments. Then insert your hand into his penis and blow on the skin, lifting it upward until the head of the penis protrudes.
Then cleanse it of any filth that may have accumulated, and tie the designated spot with a doubled thread; then tie a second ligature a short distance below it. Hold the lower ligature firmly with your thumb and index finger, and cut between the two ligatures. Then quickly lift the skin upward and expose the head of the penis, and allow the blood to flow for a short time; this is best and least likely to cause swelling of the penis. Then dry it with a damp cloth and sprinkle dry, burnt pumpkin ash over it – this is the best remedy I have found, or alternatively, powdered orris root, which is also excellent.
Then quickly lift the skin upward and expose the head of the penis, and allow the blood to flow for a short time; this is best and least likely to cause swelling of the penis. Then dry it with a damp cloth and sprinkle dry, burnt pumpkin ash over it – this is the best remedy I have found, or alternatively, powdered orris root, which is also excellent. Then apply a poultice of cooked egg white beaten with rose water and fresh rose oil to the area; leave it on for a day, and then treat it with all the usual remedies until it is healed.
And this is an image of the scissors which are suitable for cleansing.
Let it be a sharp, straight-bladed pair of scissors with a nail file and let the length of the blades be equal to the length of the handles. As for the mistake that occurs during cleansing, it may turn the whole or part of the skin inward upon cutting, so it should be stretched from your moment with your fingernail before the place swells.
Cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, pull it with a string and cut it. If three days have passed and what is under the head of the hemorrhoid remains swollen and warm, leave it until the hot swelling subsides and then remove it gently.
Cut it according to what is available to you, and preserve the head of the hemorrhoid, for if some of the head of the hemorrhoid is cut off, it will not harm that, so treat it with what heals the wound from the necessities that we have described in the article on necessities.
And if some of the skin is cut off above the amount and it shrinks upwards, that will not harm much either, so treat it as we have mentioned until it heals.
Chapter Fifty-Eight.
On the Treatment of Urine Retention in the Bladder.
Urine retention in the bladder is due to its blockage by a stone or solidified blood or pus or growing flesh and the like, so if you treat that with what we have mentioned types of treatment described in the division.
And if the urine has not been released and you see that its retention is due to a stone previously harming in the neck of the bladder, then the patient should be on his knees crouched, then ride a man on his back and extend his abdomen to his back, and let the patient himself hold as much as he can.
This will then force the neck of the bladder to push the stone back so that the urine is released. If it does not release as mentioned and the matter becomes severe for the patient, then you should use its removal with a device called a catheter, which has this image: .
It is made of silver, thin and smooth, hollow like a bird's feather quill in its delicacy, long to about a palm and a half, with a delicate funnel at its head. The way to attract urine with it is to take a doubled thread and tie a wick or cotton firmly at its end.
You insert the end of the thread into the bottom of the catheter and cut it with scissors so that a bit of the wick will enter the tube to block it like a plug. Then you grease the catheter with oil or butter or egg white, and have the patient sit on a chair.
You relax his bladder and urethra with moist ointments or warm water and oil, then gently insert the catheter into the urethra until it reaches the base of the urethra, then bend the urethra upwards towards the scrotum and push the catheter inside.
Until the urethra is bent, then push the catheter further inside until it reaches near the prostate gland. Then tilt the penis downwards with the catheter still inside and push it until it reaches the bladder. The patient will feel that it has reached something empty.
This is done in this manner because the passage through which urine flows has bends. Then, you pull the wick with the thread slightly tight so that urine follows the wick; then you remove it and urine will flow out; and repeat with another catheter.
You continue to do this until the bladder is emptied and the patient feels relief.
Chapter Ninety-Five
How to Inject the Bladder with Syringe.
The instruments suitable for this are made of silver or ivory, hollow with a long thin tube. You intend to drip water and medicine through it using an instrument called a syringe. This is its image:
It is made of silver or hollow ivory with a long tube on the narrow part, all hollow except for the end, which has three holes in it; two on one side and one on the other as you see.
The hollow space where the cannon is should be sized so that it is fully plugged, and when you pull something wet with it, it will be drawn in, and if you push it, it will be pushed away like what is done to the nozzle which throws oil in sea battles.
So if you want to introduce moisture into the bladder, insert the tip of the syringe into the moisture and draw it up with the cannon; the moisture will be drawn into the hollow of the syringe, then enter its end into the urethra as we described in the catheters, then push the moisture with the cannon.
That moisture will reach the bladder in its proper place until the patient feels it, and this is also a drawing of a delicate injector that injects the bladder:
It is made of silver or a spadroon, its top resembling a small funnel, and below it is a groove in which the ribbon is placed; then take a camel bladder and put the moisture you want to inject into the bladder in it, then tie it tightly between the grooves with a doubled thread.
Warm that moisture slightly over the fire, then insert the tip of the injector into the urethra and then pull your hand on the bladder with the moisture tightly until the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder.
If you don't have a bladder, take a piece of thin cloth and make a circle out of it, pierce it all the way around, then insert a tight string into those holes as they rotate, then gather the circle as you would gather a tablecloth after putting what you want of moisture, ointments and water in it.
Then tie it into the apparatus and do with it as you did with the bladder, squeezing your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
Chapter Sixty.
On the Extraction of the Stone.
We have mentioned in the division the types of stones and their treatment with medicine, and we have mentioned the difference between a stone generated in the kidney and a stone generated in the bladder, and the signs of all that, and we have mentioned the stone in which work is done by hand and incision.
It is the stone generated specifically in the bladder and lodged in the urethra, and I will describe it with a clear and concise explanation.
I say that the stone generated in the bladder is most common in boys, and among its signs is that urine exits the bladder resembling water in its thinness.
Sand appears in it, and its mention is scratched and tampered with, and it often dangles and then spreads, and the buttocks protrude with many of them, and boys are easily cured from it until they reach fourteen years old, and it is difficult in the elderly, while young men are moderate between that.
And the one whose stone is larger is easier to treat, and the smaller ones are the opposite. So if we turn to treatment, it should first be injected into the urethra with an injection that removes all the filth in its canal, for it may prevent the presence of the stone upon examination.
Then the urethra is taken with its legs, shaken and stirred downwards so that the stone descends to the neck of the bladder or jumps from a high place several times, then he sits between your hands upright with his hands under his thighs so that the bladder becomes all sloping downwards, then examine it.
And feel it from the outside, if you feel the stone in the space, hurry up and cut it open, if it doesn't fall under your hand at all, then you should smear the index finger of your left hand with oil if the patient is a boy or the middle finger.
If it is a healthy boy, you enter it into his seat and search for the stone until it falls under your finger. Then you move it little by little towards the neck of the bladder, then press it with your finger and push it out towards the place where you wish to cut.
You order a servant to squeeze the bladder with his hand, and you order another servant to extend his right hand over the anus and with his other hand to extend the skin under the anus towards the place where the incision will be. Then you take the dissecting forceps whose picture is this: .
You incise between the seat and the anus, not in the middle but to the side of the left testicle, and the incision should be on the same level as the stone. Your finger is in the seat while you press it outwards so that the incision is wide from the outside and narrow from the inside, as much as possible for the stone to exit.
Do not press too hard, for perhaps the finger in the seat will press the stone at the incision and it will come out without difficulty. Know that some stones may have angles and corners, making them difficult to remove.
Some are smooth and resemble an acorn, they roll easily and it is easy to remove them. If the stone has angles and corners, you should enlarge the incision a little. If it still does not come out, you must trick it, either by gripping it with a tight forceps whose tip is like a file.
This will grip the stone so that it does not slip away, or you can insert a delicate instrument with a blunted end under it. If you still cannot remove it, widen the incision a little. If blood gets in your way, cut it with a scalpel.
If there are more than one, push the largest one into the bladder opening first, then incise over it. Then push the smaller ones afterwards. You do the same if there are more than two. If it is very large, know that making a large incision over it is ignorance because it exposes the patient to one of two things:
Either he will die or he will always have the continuous dripping of urine because the place will not join at all, but try to push it out so that it comes out whole or break it with forceps so that it comes out in pieces.
Then, when you have finished your work, cauterize the wound with frankincense and patience and a bandage and tighten it, and make a poultice over it moistened with oil and syrup or rose ointment and cold water to soothe the hot swelling, then let the patient lie on his back and do not loosen the bandage until the third day.
Then, when the bandage is removed, wash the place with plenty of water and oil, then treat it with nabath ointment and basilicon ointment until it heals. If there arises in the wound a hot swelling, redness, pain, or something similar, such as blood freezing in the bladder and urine being withheld from it, which is known by the blood coming out with the urine.
Then insert your finger into the wound and remove that blood, for if it remains, it will lead to corruption of the bladder and its suppuration; then wash the wound with vinegar, water, and salt, and treat each type according to its appearance until it heals.
And it is necessary during all treatment times to bind the thighs together so that the medicines placed on the spot are fixed; if the stone is small and has entered the urethra and become embedded there, preventing urine from exiting, treat it with what I have described before it reaches the incision.
I often dispensed with this treatment, as I have tried it, and that is to take a steel iron speculum whose shape is:
Triangular with a sharp end inserted into a handle, then take a thread and tie it to the penis under the stone so that it does not return to the bladder, then gently insert the steel speculum into the urethra until the speculum reaches the same stone.
You turn the stone in your hand a little at a time while aiming to pierce it until you pass through it from the other side. Then urine will flow from its hour, and then you bind your hand on what remains of the stone outside the penis; it will crumble and come out with the urine, and the patient recovers.
If this treatment is not prepared for you, an obstacle prevents you from it, then tie a thread under the stone and another thread above the stone, then cut on the stone in the same penis between the ligatures, then remove it.
Then you loosen the ligature and cleanse the coagulated blood that has become in the wound, but it is necessary to tie the thread under the stone so that it does not return to the bladder and the other ligature above so that when the thread is loosened after the stone comes out, the skin returns to its place and covers the wound.
Therefore, it is necessary for you to lift the skin upwards when tying the upper thread so that it returns upon your release and covers the wound as we have said.
Chapter Sixty-One.
On Removing Stone for Women.
Stones rarely occur in women. If one of them suffers from a stone, its treatment is difficult and prohibited for many reasons, one of which is that the woman may be a virgin, and the second is that you will not find a woman who allows herself to be examined by a doctor.
If she is a virgin or one of those who are closely related, and third, you will not find a woman who is skilled in this craft, especially working with her hands, and fourth, the incision site for the stone in women is far from the stone's location itself, so it requires a deep incision.
There is danger in that. If necessity calls for it, then a female physician who is skilled should be taken, which is rarely found; if she is not available, ask for a chaste and kind male doctor or bring a midwife who is skilled in the affairs of women or a woman who has some indication in this craft.
She should then open it and order her to do everything she is ordered to do in the examination of the stone, starting with seeing if the woman is a virgin. If so, you should insert your finger into her vagina and search for the stone. If you find it, press it under your finger.
Then order her to be incised; if she is not a virgin and is old, order the midwife to insert her finger into the vulva of the patient and search for the stone after placing her left hand on the bladder and squeezing it very hard.
If she finds it, she should push it down from the mouth of the bladder to below as far as her strength allows until it reaches the base of the thigh; then incise her opposite the middle of the vulva at the base of the thigh from whichever side she feels the stone.
Her finger should not be removed from the stone while pressing it underneath, and the incision should be small at first; then insert the probe into that small incision. If she feels the stone, enlarge the incision as much as she knows the stone will come out of it. Know that there are many kinds of stones.
Some are small and some are large, some are smooth and some are rough, some are long and some are round, and some have branches.  Know their types so that you can determine what you want. If blood overpowers you, sprinkle powdered alum on the spot and hold it for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your work.
Continue until the stone comes out, and make sure to prepare from the instruments mentioned for removing stones in men to help you in your work. If bleeding overwhelms you and you know that the pulse of blood is from a severed artery, place the ligature on the spot.
Tighten it with ligatures, tightening them firmly and leave it, do not tamper with it again; and leave the stone and do not remove it, for you may kill the patient. Then treat the wound. When the sharpness of the blood subsides after a few days and the area becomes infected, return to your work until the stone comes out.
Chapter Sixty-Second.
On incision for watery tumors.
Watery tumors are a collection of moisture in the white membrane that lies beneath the skin of the testicle surrounding the egg, called the scrotum. It may also be in a special membrane prepared by nature on one side of the egg.
Sometimes it is mistaken for another egg, and it occurs between the skin of the testicle and the white membrane we mentioned, but this only happens rarely. These tumors arise from weakness that afflicts the testicles, which then directs this material to them, or they may develop after a blow to the testicles.
This moisture can be of many colors; it may be yellowish, reddish, dark purple, or watery white, which is the most common. The signs by which it is recognized are…
Where water collects, if it is in the white membrane we mentioned, the tumor will be roundish and slightly elongated, like an egg. The testicle will not be visible because the moisture surrounds it on all sides.
If the moisture is in a special membrane, the tumor will be roundish on one side of the testicle.
Therefore, a person may mistake it for another egg. If the moisture is between the skin of the testicle and the white membrane, it will be palpable. To determine the color of the moisture, probe the tumor with the square-shaped instrument whose image precedes this passage; judge its contents by what comes out after probing.
If we turn to treatment with iron, the patient should be ordered to undergo bloodletting if he is able, and you see that his body is full. Then, he should lie on his back on something slightly elevated and place many cloths beneath him. You should then sit to his left.
Order a servant to sit to his right, extending the patient's penis to one side of the scrotum and toward the direction of the lower abdomen. Then, take a wide scalpel and incise the skin of the scrotum lengthwise from the center toward the perineum.
The incision should be straight and parallel to the line that divides the scrotal skin in half until it reaches the white peritoneum. You should then carefully dissect it, taking care not to cut it, and your dissection should be done more from the side that is adherent to the testis.  You should extend the dissection as far as you can.
Then widen the peritoneum filled with water using a broad instrument and evacuate all the fluid.  Next, separate the edges of the incision with specula and elevate the peritoneum upward, not touching the scrotal skin that contains it. Cut the peritoneum as much as you can, either in its entirety or in pieces.
Pay particular attention to the thin side, for if you do not thoroughly cut it, you will not be safe from the water returning. If the testicle protrudes outside its skin while you are working, and after you have finished cutting the peritoneum, return it to its place and then bring the edges of the scrotal skin together with sutures.
Then treat it like any other surgical wound until it heals. But if you find that the testicle is diseased from some other condition, then you should ligate the vessels in the spermatic cord to prevent bleeding, and then cut the testicle from the spermatic cord and remove the testicle. Then treat it as we have previously described.
If the collected fluid is on both sides, know that it is hydrocele in both.  Make an incision on the other side as you did on the first, and if it seems to you that the operation can be done as one, do so, then wipe away the blood.
Insert wadding that has been steeped in oil or rose ointment into the incisions, and place another layer of wadding that has been steeped in syrup and oil over the testicles. Observe the abdomen carefully and put a folded rag, which is called a bandage, on top. Tie it from above with a bandage that has six ends in this manner:
Then two cloths are taken, sewn together and stuffed with teased wool according to this example, and the ends by which it is tied are made of cotton or damp wool. They are gathered tightly in a trouser belt, and one end is taken to the buttocks up to the back.
The second is taken towards the groin, and the ends are placed on the thighs from below, and the remaining ends are placed on the armpits. All the tightening is gathered in a trouser belt. This truss may also be made by cautery instead of incision with an iron.
It is done by taking a fine, pointed iron and cutting into the skin of the scrotum, protecting it as we have described, until the white peritoneum containing water is exposed. Then take another iron like this:
It resembles a Greek eye, then apply it to the peritoneum while protecting it until all the moisture comes out. Then stretch the peritoneum with tweezers and scrape off the containing layer with the iron and cut it as much as possible so that you eradicate all of it and preserve the testicle, do not touch it with fire.
Know that this procedure is safer and further from bleeding and better than working with an incision. If, during the incision or cautery, you encounter a hot swelling, bleeding, or anything else, you should treat it as best suits the situation as previously described.
If the patient is cowardly and cannot endure this procedure because of its ugliness, let him use a bandage as I will describe, which if it proves successful for you according to the evidence we have presented.
Since the trusses are watery, the patient should sit on a high chair and then place the swelling below with a wide spatula, making the bandage long and the opening wide so that all the water flows out. Then place cotton on the spot and tie it.
Let him dress the remainder of the wound and then treat it until it heals. If water continues to seep out when you press it, this is because the white membrane obstructs the mouth of the wound and prevents the water from escaping.
Then you should insert a goose feather or the instrument with which water is extracted from lovers' ears, the illustration of which has been presented previously, or widen the opening of the wound slightly.
Know that water may return and collect again after six months or so; if it does, press it in the same manner and the patient should rest for a few days.
Chapter Sixty-Third.
On Incisions in the Flesh and Their Treatment.
Know that incision on these fleshy parts is a great danger, often leading to death; therefore, we advise leaving them alone and avoiding any interference. I shall mention the work involved and the types of swelling.
I say that many tumors may occur in bodies, composed of tissues similar to the testicles; these arise from various causes, either from excess humors flowing into the testicles or from a blow. The color of the tumor is the same as the body and it does not contain any fluid.
The tumor may be hard, and sometimes it is stony in texture, dark-colored, and insensitive; this can occur from the complication of arteries swelling as mentioned before, or from the swelling of veins. If the swelling comes from distended arteries, you will recognize this by the dispersion of the tumor.
If you press it with your fingers, nothing will disperse; this type should not be tampered with at all. As for the swelling that comes from distended veins, it does not dissipate when pressed by the fingers. This kind may be incised, along with all other flesh.
This involves making an incision in the skin of the scrotum, then pushing the testicle upwards and removing it from the white peritoneum. You must free the spermatic cord from its vessels, tie off the vessels, and cut the spermatic cord after freeing it from all sides of the testicle; if the testicle has adhered to those growing tissues.
The egg should be removed and cut. If the adhesion is between some of the peritoneal folds or between blood vessels, all of that adhesion should be freed and cut in a circular fashion.
If the growth of flesh is in the place of adhesion that is behind, it should all be cut and the egg removed as we said. Once your work is done, dress the wound abundantly with wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then treat it with all other remedies until it heals.
Chapter Sixty-Fourth.
On the Treatment of Adhesions with a Hernia.
A hernia is a twisted swelling, somewhat resembling a bunch of grapes, with relaxation of the intestines and difficulty for the patient in movement, exercise, and walking. The treatment of this condition is very similar to what has been mentioned previously.
However, it is necessary to mention the action taken by those who came before us. I say that the patient should sit on a high chair and then push the intestine down. Then grasp the skin of the scrotum with your fingers along with the vessels that are close to the penis.
Have an assistant grasp and stretch it firmly, then make a wide incision with a sharp knife, making sure the cut is in line with the vessels until the vessels are exposed. Then dissect them from all sides as I described to you when stripping the arteries in the groin. Insert a needle with a double thread into them.
Tie it at the first place where the hernia appeared, and also tie it at the end. Then make a vertical incision in the middle along the length of the body and remove all the foul and corrupted moisture that has accumulated there.
Then treat the wound with all the remedies you would use for any other surgery that requires time to heal. There is no problem if the vessels feeding one of the intestines are cut off, as long as there are enough blood vessels remaining to nourish it. If the hernia involves all the vessels, then one of the intestines should be removed along with its vessels so that the remaining testicle does not lack nourishment. If vessels are cut before they wither and are useless.
Chapter sixty-fifth.
In the treatment of intestinal fistulas.
This fistula occurs from a rupture which appears in the extended peritoneum on the abdomen towards the groins, where the intestines protrude from the hernia into one of the groins.
This hernia is either from a rupture of the peritoneum or from its extension, and these two types occur from many causes, either a blow, a jump, a shout, lifting something heavy, and so forth. The sign, if it is from an extension of the peritoneum, is that it occurs little by little over a long period.
And it does not happen suddenly, and the tumor is level to a depth because the peritoneum compresses the intestines, and the sign, if it is from a rupture of the peritoneum, is that it occurs from the beginning with great sudden pain and the tumor appears differently under the skin nearby.
This is due to the protrusion of the intestines and its passage outside the peritoneum, and sometimes the omentum protrudes with the intestines; this fistula is called intestinal and omental. It may also be with flatulence, and pus may flow in the intestines and become lodged there, resulting in the death of the patient.
This is because it causes severe pain and rumbling, especially if pressed, and treating these types of ailments with iron is dangerous and should be avoided. The treatment plan is to order the patient to return the intestines to their inside with his hand if they return.
Then he lies on his back between your hands and raises his legs, then you extend the skin next to the groin upwards and cut all the scrotal skin lengthwise, then insert speculums into the edges of the incision according to how much is needed to open it.
The incision should be as long as the egg can come out, then you dissect the peritoneal layers under the scrotal skin until the white, firm peritoneum is exposed on all sides. Then insert your index finger into what is behind the egg.
Between the white peritoneum beneath the tunica albuginea and the second peritoneum, adhesion is released behind the testicle. Then with the right hand, it is folded into the scrotum and simultaneously the white peritoneum is extended upward with the left hand, and the testicle along with the peritoneum is elevated toward the incision.
Order the servant to extend the testicle upward and you release the adhesion behind it completely, then search with your finger to make sure there is nothing of twisted intestine in the hard white peritoneum. If you find any, push it down into the abdomen below.
Then take a needle with a thick thread twisted from ten threads and insert it at the end of the peritoneum beneath the scrotal skin, next to the incision. Then cut the ends of the twisted thread so that there are four threads. Then interlock them on top of each other solidly and tie the peritoneum we mentioned as being beneath the scrotal skin tightly on both sides. Then wind the ends of the threads and tie them securely so that nothing from the vessels supplying it can reach it. This is done so that a hot tumor does not develop and also to make a second tie outside the first one, further away by less than two fingers. After these two ties, leave a length of peritoneum beneath the scrotal skin equal to the thickness of a bone.
This is done so that a hot tumor does not develop and also to make a second tie outside the first one, further away by less than two fingers. After these two ties, leave a length of peritoneum beneath the scrotal skin equal to the thickness of a bone. Cut off the rest entirely in a circular fashion and remove the testicle with it. Then make an incision below the scrotal skin that bleeds freely as described previously, and use wool soaked in oil and place it on the wound and apply the bandage we have described.
The white peritoneum we mentioned, after it has been cut, should be cauterized carefully to prevent bleeding which often occurs. Leave the bandage until it falls off by itself. If it is slow to fall off, soak it in hot water and apply something that makes it sweat so that it will come loose.
Then treat the wound with all surgical treatments until it heals.
Chapter sixty-sixth.
In these windy hernias, I have never seen anyone dare to treat them with iron. The ancients mentioned that it should be made as we described in the hernias with a femoral ring, which is to gently tie the vessels below after the incision.
Then make an incision in the middle and treat the tumor with what opens it so that the vessels fall out and treat the wound as we mentioned until it heals.
Chapter seventy-sixth.
In a hernia that occurs in the groin.
A hernia may appear in the groin, as we have said, where it occupies a place and none of the intestine descends into the scrotum. And if any did descend, it would be slight and would always return.
But if time passes, the fissure in the peritoneum increases so that the intestine and omentum descend into the scrotum, and this occurs from the extension of the peritoneum which, as we said, is found in the groin. And this happens because the peritoneum extends, then relaxes and the place swells and protrudes. Its treatment is with cautery as previously described.
It may also be treated with iron in the following manner: Let the patient lie on his back between your hands, then make a transverse incision at the warm hernia site, about three fingers wide. Then, suture the peritoneal layers beneath the skin.
Until the underlying white peritoneum is exposed, take a ligature and place it on the spot arising from the peritoneum, pressing it deep into the abdomen. Then suture the two spots arising on either side of the ligature to the peritoneum and sew them together.
Then pull the ligature end, do not cut the peritoneum at all, and do not touch the testicle or anything else as I have taught you in the treatment of intestinal hernias. Then treat it with general surgical treatment.
If the threads break, they should be cleaned and the wound sutured until it heals. Then the peritoneum will contract and the hernia will not grow.
Silk is best in this place because it is closest to safety.
Chapter eighty-six.
In relaxation of the scrotum.
Often the skin of the scrotum relaxes in some people without the flesh inside relaxing, and its appearance is unsightly. Therefore, whoever wishes to treat it should put the patient on his back.
He should cut away all the relaxed skin on top of the tough skin, then bring together the two lips. If you wish to sew first, sew the excess relaxed skin with three or four stitches and ensure they are secure, then cut between the stitches.
Then treat it like all other surgeries until it heals and the stitches fall out.
Chapter ninety-six.
On castration.
Castration is forbidden in our law.
Therefore, I should not have mentioned it in this book of mine, but I did so for two reasons: one so that it would be known to physicians in case they are asked about it and know how to treat those afflicted by it; the other is that we often need to castrate some animals for our own benefit.
Such as rams, stallions, cats and the like of these animals. I say that castration is done in two ways: either by crushing or by incision and cutting. As for that which is done by crushing, its method is that we sit the animal in hot water until its testicles relax, soften and dangle.
Then crush them with your hand until they dissolve and are no longer discernible upon touching. As for castration by incision and cutting, it is necessary to hold the animal and press the skin of its testicles with your left hand, then tie the cords and make one incision on each testicle.
Even if the two testicles protrude, cut them off after you have skinned them, and do not leave upon them any of the tunics except the thin tunic which is on the vessels; this kind of castration is better than that which is done by crushing.
For crushing may leave some of the testes so that the animal desires copulation, then treat the wound until it heals.
Chapter Seventy.
On the Treatment of Hermaphrodites.
Hermaphrodism in men occurs in two types, one of which is when it appears below the space or in the skin of the testicles between them, a shape as if it were a woman's vulva with hair and urine may flow from the one that is in the skin of the testicles.
As for women, there is one type which occurs above the vulva on the pudendum like a small man's testicles emerging outward, one of them as if it were a man's penis and the two resembling testes; and the treatment of the three types.
The two types in men and the one type in women should have that excess flesh cut off so that its trace is removed, then it should be treated with the treatment of all other surgical wounds until it heals. As for the second type in men from which urine flows that is in the skin of the testicles, there is no work to do on it nor any benefit at all.
Chapter Seventy-One.
On the Excision of the Clitoris and the Flesh Arising from the Vulvas of Women.
The clitoris may sometimes grow beyond the natural size until it becomes prominent and unsightly, and in some women it may even enlarge to such an extent that it resembles that of a man's and can cause copulation.
Therefore, the excess of the clitoris should be grasped with your hand or forceps and cut off, without being too deep in the incision, especially at the root so as not to cause bleeding.
Then treat it with the treatment of wounds until it is healed, and as for the growing flesh, it is flesh that grows in the mouth of the womb until it fills it.
And perhaps it protrudes outward like a tail. Therefore, some of the ancients call it the taillike disease, so it should be cut off as the penis is cut off, and treated until it heals.
Chapter Seventy-Two.
In the Treatment of Prolapsus.
Prolapsus is when a woman's vulva is not pierced or the hole is small, and it is either natural, with which she was born, or incidental, which arises from a previous cause. Incidental prolapsus comes from an excess of fleshy growth.
Or it is from thin or thick peritoneum, which may be found deep in the uterus, at its sides, above it, or below it, and it prevents intercourse, conception, childbirth, and sometimes menstruation. Recognition of this condition is made by a midwife through examination.
If the obstruction is visible and nearby, and if it is not visible, examine it with her fingers or a speculum. If the obstruction is from thin peritoneum and is close to the labia, proceed to pierce it. Do this by placing something resembling stirrups on the labia, then place both thumbs of both hands together.
The woman should be lying on her back with her legs spread, then stretch the labia forcefully until the thin peritoneum is pierced and the obstruction opens. Then take some wool, soak it in oil, and place it on the area. Have intercourse with the woman every day so that the area does not heal together again.
If the peritoneum is thick and dense, it should be cut with a wide spatula resembling an aspen leaf. If the obstruction is from fleshy growth, hang it with forceps and cut it off. Have pain-relieving medications on hand that do not cause burning, such as gum arabic, mastic, frankincense mixed together with egg white.
Then a wide lead tube is used so that the wound does not heal quickly, it is held for several days and a dry linen wick is used, then it is treated with all the treatment of fusion until it heals, and if another piece of flesh grows in the womb, it should be cut in this manner.
Unless it is a cancerous tumor, a cancerous tumor in the womb is not treated with iron at all.
Chapter Seventy-Third.
In the treatment of hemorrhoids, warts and red pimples that appear in the vulvas of women.
Hemorrhoids are a swelling of the veins until a lot of blood flows from them constantly, and if hemorrhoids develop, they become warts, and I have mentioned their types and signs in the classification, and we will mention them here.
What can be treated from it and what cannot be treated, I say that hemorrhoids and warts, if they are deep in the womb and do not appear to touch, there is no treatment for them with iron, and what is in the mouth of the womb and touches it is what is treated.
The woman should enter a cold house, then extend the warts with a scraper or a coarse rag and cut them from their roots, then put on it, when blood flows, one of the hemostatic astringents without lubrication.
Such as quince, rue, frankincense and the like, then raise her legs to the wall for an hour, then lower them into cold water, if the bleeding continues, sit her in a decoction of senna, pomegranate peel and henna and the like, then take barley flour, knead it with honey and vinegar.
And bandage it on her back, if the bleeding stops, otherwise insist on pressing the breasts and nipples without any conditions, then take a wick and dip it in the juice of purslane or the juice of lamb's tongue or the juice of willow branches with henna syrup and apply it to the place.
If the swelling subsides, treat the area with ointment until it heals. As for the red wart, it resembles the heads of millet, rough in appearance. It should be cut off as described for calluses and treated until it heals.
Chapter Seventy-Four.
On the incision of a carbuncle that appears in the uterus.
Many types of tumors can appear in the uterus, such as cancer, stony tumors, ulcers, fistulas, gangrene, warts, hemorrhoids, fissures, and hot tumors. I have mentioned all these diseases, their types, and their signs in the division.
In this article, we should mention the hot tumor that appears in the uterus if it is one of the tumors that collects for a period of time and how to incise it with iron. It should be examined to see if the pain in the beginning of the tumor is sharp with pulsating, inflammation, and fever.
And if you see it red when touched, do not rush to incise it and treat it with what helps ripening until these symptoms subside. Then, the woman should sit on a chair with two seats and lean on her back.
Gather her legs towards the lower abdomen and let her thighs be parted. Her arms should be placed under her knees and tied with a suitable band.
Therefore, the midwife sits on the right side and uses the instrument that opens the cervix, whose image will come later. If you want to use this instrument, estimate the depth of the woman's uterus so that what enters from the instrument does not exceed the depth of the uterus.
If the instrument is deeper than necessary, it will harm the patient. Therefore, pads should be placed on the lip of the cervix to prevent the entire instrument from entering the depth of the uterus. The spiral that runs in the instrument should be at the top side.
And you hold the instrument while the servant turns the screw until the neck of the womb is opened; then, when the abscess appears and is touched by the hand, if it is soft and delicate, it should be cut at its head with a broad scalpel. And when all the matter has been discharged.
A soft wick should then be put into the wound, soaked in rose oil or green oil with some astringents; and the wick should come out of the incision in the neck of the womb, and pure wool soaked in water which has been boiled with baker's yeast should be applied externally on the womb and the pudendum.
Then it should be treated after two days with a salve suitable for that purpose until it heals.
And the womb and the wound may be washed by injecting it with water and honey, then with water which has been boiled with the root of marshmallow or long angelica; and it should return to the salve afterwards. If the abscess is hidden inside the womb.
The use of iron for its treatment should be avoided, but it should be treated as mentioned in the division above.
Chapter Seventy-Fifth.
On teaching midwives how to treat living fetuses if they are born in an unnatural way.
The midwife should first know the signs of natural childbirth. These are: When a woman feels pressure downward and longs to smell the air, it becomes easier for her to endure labor.
The fetus is quickly expelled. Know that this childbirth occurs in a natural manner, and the fetus emerges headfirst with the placenta either accompanying it or hanging from its cord. If you see these signs, pressure should be applied to her abdomen so the fetus exits quickly.
If it descends onto his head, the placenta will descend with it and be cleansed of those superfluities well. And besides this birth, it is unnatural and blameworthy because the fetus may come out on its feet and put out its hands before its head and legs.
Or one of his hands or one of his feet may come out, or his head and hand may come out, or he may come out folded, and perhaps turn on his back, and so forth from these blameworthy shapes. Therefore, the midwife should be skillful and gentle with all these things and beware of error and mistakes.
And I will explain each shape and how to manage it so that you can recognize it and act accordingly. If the fetus comes out headfirst, which is the natural way, and this is difficult for the woman and labor is prolonged, and you see her strength has weakened, seat her on a chair and order women to hold her steady.
And apply a poultice of cooked fenugreek and soft ointments to her womb, then the midwife inserts a small speculum between her fingers and makes an incision in the placenta with it, or cuts it with her fingernail until the moisture inside flows out, and she presses on the woman's abdomen until the fetus descends.
If it does not descend, the woman should be injected with a fenugreek decoction mixed with sesame oil, and then after the injection she should be made to cough and sneeze by tickling her with a feather while her mouth and nose are held shut; for the fetus will come out at that moment. If the fetus's hand comes out first, it should be gently pushed back in little by little.
If entry is not possible, place the woman on a raised platform and raise her legs above it, then shake the platform on the ground while holding the woman so she does not fall during the shaking. If the hands still do not enter and the fetus is dead, cut off its hands and draw out the rest of the fetus.
Or bind his hands with a cloth and pull them moderately, for he will come out, exiting on his legs. If the fetus exits on its legs, it is necessary to push them upwards and then turn the fetus little by little until it is straightened. Then take one of its legs and extend it little by little.
If they come out to the thighs, order her to move and push it with the hand, for it will come out. If it does not come out as we have described, or otherwise return the fetus a little until it becomes in its natural form, then it will come out smoothly. If it refuses what we have all described.
Take saliva of rue, saliva of fenugreek, sheep tallow and frankincense dissolved and beat all together in a mortar very well. Then apply it to the woman's vulva and lower abdomen, then sit her in lukewarm water until she reaches the climax.
If you see that her lower part has loosened, make a suppository for her of rue and let her hold it. If she holds the suppository for an hour, then seat her on a chair, and push her and cover her mouth and nose and squeeze her lower abdomen lightly, for the fetus will come out in its time, exiting on its knees and hands.
If it comes out in this way, take care to insert its hands little by little, then let the woman lie on her back and lower her legs down while she is lying on a bed with her hands held together. Then squeeze over her abdomen lightly. Then remove what is under her legs from the pillows so that her lower body is upright. If the fetus does not come out, take hold of both her legs and move them strongly. Then squeeze over the pubis lightly until the fetus ascends upwards. Then let the midwife insert her hand and straighten the fetus little by little.
And order the woman to recline so that the fetus comes out, the coming out of the fetus being opposed and delayed because one of its hands is stuck.  Seize the hand and push it back; if she is unable to push it back, make the woman stand and have her walk; if she is unable to walk, then lay her down on...
...her bed and shake her legs vigorously, then use the pessary that I have described from the speculums; if she is seized by a contraction, then seat her on a chair and then proceed to push back the hand and straighten the fetus into its natural form.  Make the woman sneeze and order her to recline so that it comes out.
If the fetus comes out on its head with its arms outstretched and its face toward its mother's back, the midwife should grasp the fetus' hand and then turn it a little at a time, straightening it gently.  And if it becomes straightened, apply to the mother's vulva what we have described of oil and speculums.
Then encourage her to move a little at a time; and if she does that, seat her on a chair and order her to lean to her right side, then encourage her to recline and make her sneeze with candied fruit (kandus), for it will come out. If the fetus comes out standing upright on its side.
If it descends into the mouth of the womb in this manner with the placenta, tear the placenta with your fingernail until it is emptied of moisture; if it clings to the face and neck of the fetus, cut it from the origin so that it does not suffocate and die, then push the fetus back inside until you make it right.
And order the woman to recline several times, for it will come out easily. Regarding twins or multiple births, know that twins very often are born and three or four may also be born and live, though this is rare.  As for five, it is something outside of nature and they do not live at all.
And they are surrounded by a single placenta, even if they are numerous, and they are separated by a dividing septum between them, attached at the base of each one of them. And they may be delivered as a single fetus is delivered easily and naturally, or they may be delivered in a monstrous delivery, as we have described.
If one of them becomes obstructed during delivery and assumes one of the unnatural forms we have mentioned, then treat it as we have described. And let the midwife be gentle and do what she does carefully and patiently, and devise a plan for every form that presents itself to her, leading to safety.
Remember that fetuses conceived in the womb may be miscarried; there may be one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, or more than ten conceived.  It has been confirmed to me that a woman miscarried seven and another fifteen, all of them conceived.
By the estimation of the Most Wise, All-Knowing One, all of this should be known by the midwife, for she may encounter such a situation someday and thus deal with it appropriately.
Chapter Seventy-Six.
On the Extraction of a Stillborn Fetus.
If you have treated the stillborn fetus as mentioned in the section on treatment and it has not been delivered, and you are compelled to proceed manually, then you should examine her. If the woman is healthy and strong and does not exhibit any symptoms that might endanger her, she should lie on a bed on her back.
Her head should be inclined downwards, and her legs should be raised; an attendant should hold her steady from both sides, or she may be tied to the bed so that her body does not move when the fetus is extracted.
Then the midwife should moisten the mouth of her uterus with soft ointments, composed of mallow sap, fenugreek, and flaxseed; then she should anoint her hands with these ointments and saliva, and gently insert them into the uterus. Then she should seek a location where to insert the forceps on the fetus and corresponding places.
Look and see if the fetus is coming out head first, then insert pins into its eyes or temples or mouth or palate or under its chin or collarbone or in places near the ribs or under the shoulder blades.
But if it is coming out feet first, then in the groin and the middle ribs; and you should hold the pin in your right hand and make its loop between the fingers of your left hand, insert your hand gently and embed a pin in some of those places that we have mentioned.
Until you reach something hollow, then embed another pin or a third if needed so that the traction is equal and does not lean to one side; then extend it evenly and do not make the extension only straight but move it to every direction.
To make it come out easily as is done with a molar when it is extracted; and in between that, the extension should be slackened. If one side becomes stuck, then the midwife should smear some fingers with oil and insert them from that side to turn what is stuck. If part of the fetus comes out, then move the pins to other places.
She should lift it a little to do this until the whole fetus comes out; if a hand comes out before anything else and cannot be pushed back due to compression, then a rag should be wrapped around it and pulled until it all comes out, after which it is cut.
Either at the wrist joint or at the elbow; and thus it should be done with the other hand and the legs. If the fetus's head is large and experiences pressure during delivery, or if there is accumulated water in its head, then a pointed forceps should be inserted between the fingers.
And pierce the head with it so that the water comes out, or insert it with a device called a trephine, the image of which comes with the images of all other instruments in the chapter that follows this one.
Likewise, if the fetus has a large head by nature, the skull should be cut or crushed with a forceps as we have said, and then the bones should be extracted with forceps. If the head comes out and is compressed at the neck, it should be cut until the moisture in the chest drains.
Then the chest will contract; but if it does not contract and delivery is not possible, cut as much as you can. If the lower abdomen is warm or contains pus, it should be punctured so that the moisture drains from it.
If the fetus is on its legs, pulling it out is easy and straightening it to the mouth of the womb is simple. But if it is compressed at the abdomen or chest, it should be pulled with a cloth wrapped around your hand and the abdomen or chest should be cut so that what is inside flows out.
If all the other limbs are removed and the head returns and is stuck, let the midwife insert her left hand. If the mouth of the womb is open, she should insert her hand into the cervix, seek out the head with it, and pull it towards the mouth of the womb with her fingers; then she should insert a spoon or two spoons and pull with them.
If the mouth of the womb has closed due to a hot, inflamed tumor, it should not be forced. Instead, wet, fatty substances should be poured on it, poultices should be applied, and she should sit in water that softens and moistens.
If the fetus is on its side and can be straightened, use what we have mentioned for a living fetus. If this is not possible, cut it in pieces and remove it.  Nothing of the placenta should be left inside at all. After you have finished your treatment, apply what we have mentioned for treating hot tumors that occur in the womb.
If bleeding occurs, she should immerse herself in astringent water and use all other treatments. I have seen a woman who became pregnant, the fetus died inside her, and then she became pregnant again.
Then the other fetus also died, and after a long time she developed a tumor in her abdomen which swelled until it opened and began to discharge pus. She was called for treatment and I treated her for a long time but the wound did not close, so I applied some strong drawing ointments to it.
A bone then came out of the place, and after some days another bone came out. I was astonished by this, for the abdomen is a place where there are no bones. I concluded that they were from the bones of the dead fetus, so I searched the wound and removed many bones from it, bones of the head of the fetus.
I continued to do this until I removed many bones from it, and the woman was in the best of health. She lived for a long time, with a small amount of pus still discharging from the place. Indeed, I have only brought this rare case here.
For it contains knowledge and assistance for what the physician, the maker with his hand, attempts in treatment.
Chapter Seventy-Seventh.
It contains images of the instruments needed for extracting a fetus.

This is the instrument with which books are bound, it has two screws at the ends of the wooden pieces except that this screw should be finer than the one for binding books and should be either ebony or boxwood, and each piece of wood should be as thick as two fingers.
And their curve is towards a finger, and their length is a palm and a half. In the middle of the two pieces of wood are two ridges of the same wood, which have been firmly fixed into them; their length is half a palm or a little more, and their width is about two fingers or a little more. These two ridges...
are what enter the mouth of the womb to open it when you turn the screws. Image of another instrument similar to that, but finer and lighter:
It is made of ebony or boxwood in the shape of callipers, but it has two points at its end as you see, each point being about a span long and two fingers wide. If you wish to open the uterus with it.
Seat the woman on a bed with her legs spread apart, then insert these two points into the mouth of the uterus while holding the handle of the instrument below between her thighs. Then open your hand as you do with callipers, to whatever extent you wish to open the uterus. So that the midwife can achieve what she wants.
